Town Dweller Selling for Bedouin (Bay' al-Hadir lil-Badi)
Ruling and hadith proof for prohibition of town dweller acting as broker for Bedouin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for bay' al-hadir lil-badi and identify the condition that changes its permissibility.

Core Idea
A town dweller may not broker for a Bedouin if it harms townspeople; otherwise permissible.

This lesson addresses the second prohibited sale in the chapter: a town dweller selling for a Bedouin. The primary evidence is the hadith from Ibn Abbas. Understanding the condition of harm is crucial to correctly applying this ruling, as the prohibition is not absolute but conditional.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a town dweller (hadir) acting as a broker (simsar) for a Bedouin (badi) who brings goods to town. The ruling is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) if it harms townspeople; otherwise permissible.
The ruling is not absolute; harm is decisive.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas (ra) narrated in Bukhari and Muslim: 'Do not intercept the riders, and let not a town dweller sell for a Bedouin.'
The hadith is mutafaq 'alayh, but its meaning requires interpretation.
3
Understand the interpretation
Ibn Abbas explained 'sell for a Bedouin' as being a broker (simsar) or middleman (dallal). This is the standard Hanafi understanding.
The prohibition applies specifically to brokerage, not to ordinary sales between town and Bedouin.
4
Note the condition of harm
The author gives two scenarios: (1) the town dweller sells the Bedouin's goods later at a higher price, (2) from Sharh al-Tahawi: selling food to Bedouins at high prices during a drought harming townspeople. In both cases, harm triggers prohibition; without harm, it is permissible.
Harm can be price inflation or shortage for townspeople.
5
Apply to scenarios
Use the condition of harm to evaluate any similar situation. If the transaction disadvantages the local community, it is makruh tahrimi; if not, it is permissible.
This ruling balances free trade and public welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيع الحاضر للبادي: لما روي عن ابن عباس الله ما أنه قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "لا تتلقوا الركبان، ولا يبع حاضر لباد"، فقيل لابن عباس: ما معنى قوله : "لا يبع حاضر لباد؟ فقال: لا يكون الحاضر سمسار البادي، أي دلالاً، رواه البخاري ومسلم وصورته أن يجلب البادي السلعة، فيأخذها الحاضر ليبيعها عن جانبه بعد الوقت بأعلى من السعر الموجود وقت الجلب. وفي "شرح الطحاوي صورته أن الرجل إذا كان له طعام وأهل المصر في قحط، يبيعه من أهل المصر وهو لا في قحط حتى يتوسعوا ولكن يبيعه من أهل البادية بثمن غال وأهل المصر يتضررون بذلك، فلا يجوز، وإن كانوا لا يتضررون بذلك، فلا بأس ببيعه منهم. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٥/٢]
And the sale of a town dweller for a Bedouin: because it is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not intercept the riders, and let not a town dweller sell for a Bedouin.' It was said to Ibn Abbas: What is the meaning of his statement 'let not a town dweller sell for a Bedouin'? He said: The town dweller should not be a broker for the Bedouin, i.e., a middleman. Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. Its description: The Bedouin brings goods, and the town dweller takes them to sell them on his behalf later at a price higher than the current market price at the time of import. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: Its description is that if a man has food and the townspeople are in drought, he sells it to the townspeople while he is not in drought so that they may become comfortable, but he sells it to the Bedouins at a high price, and the townspeople are harmed by that; then it is not permissible. If they are not harmed, then there is no harm in selling to them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 45/2]
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage explains the second disliked sale: a town dweller selling for a Bedouin (bay' al-hadir lil-badi). The primary proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas in Bukhari and Muslim: 'Do not intercept the riders, and let not a town dweller sell for a Bedouin.' Ibn Abbas interprets the second part as the town dweller acting as a broker (simsar) or middleman (dallal) for the Bedouin. The prohibition is because the town dweller, knowing local prices, can exploit the situation by selling the Bedouin's goods later at a higher price, or by selling to Bedouins when townspeople are in need. The author cites two descriptions: one where the town dweller takes the goods to sell later at a profit, and another from Sharh al-Tahawi where the issue is selling food to Bedouins at high prices while townspeople suffer drought. The ruling is that such sale is not permissible (la yajuz) if it harms the townspeople; otherwise, it is permissible. This reflects the Hanafi principle of public welfare and prevention of harm.

Key Terms
حاضر (hadir): A town dweller, one who resides in a settled area (misr).
بادي (badi): A Bedouin, a desert dweller who comes to town to sell goods.
سمسار (simsar): A broker or middleman who mediates a sale for commission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it prohibited for a town dweller to sell for a Bedouin?
A) Always, regardless of circumstances.
B) Only when the town dweller acts as a broker without the Bedouin's permission.
C) When it harms the townspeople by causing shortage or higher prices.
D) Only during drought.

Key Takeaway
Bay' al-hadir lil-badi is makruh tahrimi only if it harms the townspeople; otherwise it is permissible.

Bidding Up (Najsh) and Separating Family: Prohibited Sales
Brief ruling with hadith proof against bidding up (najsh).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bidding up (najsh), identify its dalil from hadith, and explain why it is prohibited.

Core Idea
Bidding up without intention to buy is haram, as it deceives and is linked to family separation.

This lesson addresses the prohibition of a specific deceptive sale: bidding up (bay' man yazid), also known as najsh. The text connects it to the broader prohibition of separating close relatives, citing a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding this ruling protects one from engaging in a transaction that, while outwardly valid, carries sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that 'bay' man yazid' refers to someone bidding up the price in an auction with no intention to purchase, just to deceive. The ruling is haram.
The text uses the negation 'la' for emphasis.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Abu Musa narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni: the Prophet cursed those who separate a mother and child or brother and brother.
The hadith is ahad but accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does cursing those who separate family prove prohibition of najsh? The text explicitly includes bay' man yazid as a means of separation. The curse indicates a major sin (kabirah).
The link is explicit: the author states that separation includes sale by bidding up.
4
Note the scope
The prohibition applies to Muslims (free, mukatab, or slave permitted to trade) but not to disbelievers, as they are not addressed by Islamic rulings.
However, the sin remains in itself.
5
Understand the emphasis
The phrase 'la bay'a man yazid' uses 'la' for exaggeration in prohibition, not literal negation of the sale's validity. The sale is valid but the bidder sins.
This is similar to 'la salah li jar' meaning 'no prayer for the neighbor' indicating strong prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بيع من يزيد لما . روي عن أنس عنه أن رسول الله باع قدحا وجلساً ولا يفرق يعني المسلم، حراً كان أو مكاتباً أو مأذونا له في التجارة، بخلاف الكافر؛ لأن الكفار غير مخاطبين بالشرائع، عبر بالنفي مبالغة في المنع؛ إذ قد ورد عن أبي موسى قال: لعن رسول الله الله من فرق بين الوالدة وولدها، وبين الأخ وأخيه، رواه ابن ماجه والدار قطني. والمراد التفريق ببيع أو هبة أو قسمة ميراد راث أو غنيمة أو بيع من يزيد. (عناية)
No sale by bidding up (bay' man yazid) because it is narrated from Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sold a cup and a cloth... And he (the seller) should not separate [family] meaning the Muslim, whether free, a mukatab, or one permitted to trade, unlike the disbeliever because disbelievers are not addressed by the divine laws. The negation is used for exaggeration in prohibition. Since it has been narrated from Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) cursed the one who separates between a mother and her child, and between a brother and his brother. Narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni. And what is meant is separation by sale, gift, division of inheritance, spoils, or sale by bidding up. (al-'Inayah)
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage covers two related issues: 'no sale by bidding up' (la bay'a man yazid) and prohibition of separating family members. The text first mentions the hadith from Anas about the Prophet selling a cup and cloth, but the emphasis is on the phrase 'la bay'a man yazid' which refers to the practice of bidding up in an auction without intending to buy (najsh). This is prohibited because it deceives the seller and other bidders. The text then connects this to the prohibition of separating close relatives by sale, citing the hadith from Abu Musa where the Prophet cursed those who separate a mother from her child or a brother from his brother. The author notes that this applies to Muslims, whether free, mukatab (slave with contract of manumission), or a slave permitted to trade, but not to disbelievers as they are not obligated by Islamic rulings (though the sin may still exist). The negation 'la' is used to emphasize strong prohibition. The text further states that the prohibition includes separation by sale, gift, division of inheritance, spoils, or even by bidding up. This shows that the rules are interconnected.

Key Terms
بيع من يزيد (bay' man yazid): An auction where someone bids up the price without intending to buy, to deceive others.
نجش (najsh): The act of bidding up without intention to purchase, to inflate price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is makruh tanzihi.
C) It is haram.
D) It is wajib to stop such bidding.

Key Takeaway
Bidding up without intent to buy (najsh) is haram and incurs a curse; the sale itself is valid but the bidder sins.

The Ruling on Selling During Friday Adhan
Ruling with Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling during the Friday adhan and explain the Quranic evidence from Surah al-Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Selling during the first Friday adhan is makruh tahrimi; the contract is valid but sinful.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on conducting a sale when the Friday adhan is called. The primary evidence is the Qur'anic command to 'leave off trade.' We will see how this yields a ruling of prohibition (makruh tahrimi) without invalidating the contract, and clarify the timing and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Selling during the Friday adhan. The Hanafi school rules it as makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The sale itself is valid but the action is sinful.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
The proof is Qur'an 62:9: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade.' The operative phrase is 'leave off trade' (wa dharu al-bay').
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'dharu' (leave) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarina. Here, the context of Friday prayer makes leaving trade wajib, implying prohibition of the act.
The command to leave does not necessarily invalidate the contract itself; only the act is prohibited.
4
Note the conditions and exceptions
The adhan considered is the first adhan after zawal (noon). Some scholars (Abu al-Yusr) allowed the sale if walking, but this is not accepted. The prohibition applies only to those obligated to attend Jumu'ah.
Those exempt from Jumu'ah (e.g., travelers, women) may trade during the adhan.
5
State the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view: sale is valid but makruh tahrimi. It is sinful to contract but the contract is enforceable.
Malik and Ahmad rule the sale invalid, but Hanafis differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبيع عند أذان الجمعة [الأول إلا إذا تبايعا وهما يمشيان فلا بأس به. عيني)] لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَذَرُوا الْبَيْعَ﴾ (الجمعة:٩) لأن فيه إخلالاً بواجب السعي الذي أمر الله به بقوله: ﴿فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ الله﴾ (الجمعة:٩) ولهذا قال أبو اليسر: لو تبايعا وهما يمشيان، فلا بأس به، وهذا مشكل؛ لأن الله تعالى قد نهى عن البيع مطلقاً، فمن جوزه في بعض الوجوه يكون تخصيصاً، وهو نسخ فلا يجوز، وقد خص منه من لا جمعة عليه، والأذان المعتبر في تحريم البيع هو الأول إذا وقع بعد الزوال على المختار، وعند مالك وأحمد: لا ينعقد البيع أصلاً. ثم اعلم أن الآية ليس فيها نهي، وإنما فيه الأمر بترك البيع، لكن لما كان الأمر بتركه مستلزماً للنهي عنه أطلق الأمر على النهي. (عيني، فتح)
And sale at the time of the Friday adhan [the first, except if they transact while walking, then there is no harm. ('Ayni)] due to His statement: ﴾And leave off trade﴿ (al-Jumu'ah:9) because it involves violation of the obligation of proceeding (sa'y) which Allah commanded in His saying: ﴾So proceed to the remembrance of Allah﴿ (al-Jumu'ah:9). For this reason Abu al-Yusr said: If they transact while walking, there is no harm. But this is problematic because Allah has prohibited sale absolutely. Whoever allows it in some respects is making a specification, which is abrogation, not permissible. And it has been specified for those upon whom Friday is not obligatory. The adhan considered for prohibition of sale is the first, if it occurs after noon (zawal) according to the chosen view. According to Malik and Ahmad: the sale does not take effect at all. Then know that the verse does not contain a prohibition; rather it contains the command to leave trade. But since the command to leave it necessitates prohibition, the command is used to express prohibition. (al-'Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage discusses the third disliked sale: selling at the time of the Friday adhan. The proof is Qur'an 62:9: 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on Friday, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade.' The author explains that the adhan considered is the first adhan after zawal (noon). There is a report from Abu al-Yusr that if the two parties transact while walking to the mosque, it is permissible. But the author finds this problematic because the verse commands leaving trade absolutely. Specifying a case (walking) would be a type of abrogation (naskh) which is not valid without evidence. The prohibition only applies to those obligated to attend Friday prayer; others are excluded. The verse is not a direct prohibition but a command to leave, which implies prohibition. The schools of Malik and Ahmad go further, holding that such a sale is invalid entirely. The Hanafi position is that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to contract a sale during that time, but the contract is not invalid (batil) unless one argues otherwise. The relied-upon view is that the sale is makruh, not batil, as long as it does not involve overt violation of the command.

Key Terms
أذان الجمعة (adhan al-jumu'ah): The first call to Friday prayer after the sun passes its zenith (zawal).
السعي (sa'y): Proceeding or hastening to the Friday prayer, which is wajib.
مكروه تحريمي (makruh tahrimi): Prohibitively disliked; an action that should be avoided and is sinful, but not as severe as haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a sale conducted during the first Friday adhan after zawal?
A) The sale is invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
B) The sale is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) The sale is permissible if the parties are walking.
D) The sale is valid only if the seller is not obligated to attend Friday prayer.

Key Takeaway
Selling during the first Friday adhan is makruh tahrimi; the contract is valid but the act is sinful due to neglecting the command to proceed to prayer.

Disputes on Selling During Friday Adhan
Inter- and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement (Abu al-Yusr) and the cross-madhhab disagreement (Malik/Ahmad), and evaluate the Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
The sale during Friday adhan is subject to ikhtilaf: Abu al-Yusr permitted it if walking; Malik and Ahmad deem it invalid; the Hanafi majority rules it valid but makruh.

While the Hanafi school holds a clear position on selling during the Friday adhan, there are notable differences within the school and across madhhabs. This lesson explores the reasoning of Abu al-Yusr, who allowed the sale if both parties are walking, and the positions of Malik and Ahmad, who consider the sale invalid. We will examine the Hanafi response and understand why the majority view prevails.

Guided Path
1
State the intra-Hanafi position of Abu al-Yusr
Abu al-Yusr held that if the two parties transact while walking to the mosque, the sale is permissible (no prohibition). He likely reasoned that walking indicates they are already proceeding to prayer, so the command to leave trade is satisfied.
2
Identify the author's critique
The author rejects this as problematic. He argues that the Qur'an commands leaving trade absolutely (mutlaqan). Allowing it in some cases (walking) would be an unjustified specification (takhsis) without evidence, which is equivalent to abrogation (naskh) and thus invalid.
Takhsis without proof is not permitted in Hanafi usul.
3
State the cross-madhhab position of Malik and Ahmad
According to Malik and Ahmad, a sale conducted during the Friday adhan is invalid (batil) and does not take effect. They interpret the command to leave trade as implying the nullity of the contract.
4
Compare the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the verse commands leaving trade but does not explicitly annul the contract. Prohibition of an action does not automatically invalidate the contract; validity is determined by other principles (e.g., absence of gharar, consent). Thus, the sale remains valid.
Hanafis distinguish between hukm taklifi (obligation/prohibition) and hukm wad'i (validity).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Under Hanafi law, the contract is enforceable; under Maliki/Hanbali law, it is void. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi majority view, as it is based on sound usul and is the most reliable transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway

Prohibition of Separating Family Members: Conditions and Disputes
Ruling on separating family members by sale with conditions and internal dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which separating a minor from a mahram relative by sale is prohibited and identify the relied-upon Hanafi ruling regarding the validity of the sale.

Core Idea
Separating a minor from a mahram relative is prohibited by hadith; the sale itself may be valid but makruh tahrimi.

The Hanafi school addresses the delicate balance between property rights and family bonds. This lesson unpacks the hadith prohibiting the separation of close relatives, focusing on when the act is prohibited and how it affects the validity of the sale. We'll navigate the conditions, exceptions, and an important internal difference among Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hadith Proof
Locate the hadith from Abu Musa that the Prophet cursed the one who separates a mother from her child or a brother from his brother. Understand that this is an ahad hadith, making the ruling zanni in both transmission and meaning.
The curse indicates the act is a major sin, but does it automatically invalidate the contract?
2
Determine the Scope and Conditions
The prohibition applies only when a Muslim separates a minor (saghir) from a mahram relative they both own. The mahram must be one with permanent marriage prohibition (mu'abbad), and both must be under the same ownership.
Exceptions include separate ownership and legal rights like debt or crime.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one invalidates the sale only for direct blood lineage (qarabat al-wilad), another invalidates for all mahrams. Zufar, Abu Hanifa, and Muhammad agree with the second. However, later authorities (al-'Ayni) prefer the view that the sale is valid but makruh tahrimi.
The Prophet's treatment of Mariyah and Sirin (adult sisters) shows that adult sisters can be separated, indicating the text is 'ala khilaf al-qiyas.
4
Conclude with the Mufta Bihi Position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that the sale is valid but makruh tahrimi. The hadith's curse implies a sin but not invalidity. The seller should avoid such separation unless necessary.
This tarjih is confirmed by al-'Ayni and Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يفرق يعني المسلم، حراً كان أو مكاتباً أو مأذونا له في التجارة، بخلاف الكافر؛ لأن الكفار غير مخاطبين بالشرائع، عبر بالنفي مبالغة في المنع؛ إذ قد ورد عن أبي موسى قال: لعن رسول الله الله من فرق بين الوالدة وولدها، وبين الأخ وأخيه، رواه ابن ماجه والدار قطني. والمراد التفريق ببيع أو هبة أو قسمة ميراد راث أو غنيمة أو وصية.  بين صغير وذي رحم محرم منه، بخلاف الكبيرين والزوجين. وذي رحم محرم منه سواء كان صغيراً أو كبيراً، كافراً أو مسلماً، أو أحدهما مسلم والآخر كافر، وهذه الكراهة تمتد إلى البلوغ، والمراد بذي الرحم المحرم ما كانت القرابة فيه مؤبدة بالمحرمية، مثل الأب والابن، والأم والابن، والأخوين، فلا يدخل فيه محرم غير قريب ولا قريب غير محرم، ثم لابد من اجتماعهما في ملكه، حتى لو كان أحدهما له، والآخر لابنه الصغير ، له أن يبيع أحدهما لتفرق الملك، وكذلك لو كان التفريق بحق مستحق عليه كدفع أحدهما بالجناية، وبيع أحدهما بالدين ورده بالعيب وعن أبي يوسف أنه يفسد البيع في قرابة الولاد، ويجوز في غيرها، وعنه أنه يفسد في الجميع لما روينا، وبه قال زفر والثلاثة. بخلاف الكبيرين والزوجين سواء كانا صغيرين أو لا، فإنه لا يكره تفريقهما؛ لأن النص ورد في منع تفريق صغير عن ذي رحم محرم منه، فالكبيران والزوجان ليسا في معنى المنصوص عليه، فيجوز تفريقهما، ولا يجوز أن يثبت فيهما المنع إلحاقاً بالمنصوص عليه بالدلالة؛ لأن النص ورد على خلاف القياس، فلا يلحق به غيره بالدلالة، أن المقوقس القبطي أهدى له له مارية وسيرين و كانتا أختين، ففرق بينهما حيث تسرى بمارية، وأعطى الأخرى لحسان خلافا لمحمد. (عيني، فتح)
And he (the seller) should not separate [family] meaning the Muslim, whether free, a mukatab, or one permitted to trade, unlike the disbeliever because disbelievers are not addressed by the divine laws. The negation is used for exaggeration in prohibition. Since it has been narrated from Abu Musa (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) cursed the one who separates between a mother and her child, and between a brother and his brother. Narrated by Ibn Majah and al-Daraqutni. And what is meant is separation by sale, gift, division of inheritance, spoils, or bequest. [PAGE_306] Between a minor and a mahram relative, unlike two adults and spouses. And a mahram relative, whether minor or adult, disbeliever or Muslim, or one Muslim and the other disbeliever. And this dislikedness extends until puberty. What is meant by mahram relative (dhi rahim muharram) is one whose relationship is permanently one of mahramiyya, like father and son, mother and son, and two brothers. It does not include a non-relative mahram (like a foster relative) nor a relative who is not mahram. Then it is necessary that both be in his ownership. So if one belongs to him and the other to his minor son, he may sell one due to separation of ownership. Similarly, if the separation is due to an established right, like handing over one for a crime, or selling one for debt, or returning one due to a defect. And from Abu Yusuf: he invalidates the sale in cases of blood relation (qarabat al-wilad) but permits in others. And from him (another narration): he invalidates in all cases because of what we narrated, and Zufar and the three (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Zufar?) also said that. Unlike two adults and spouses, whether both are minors or not, for it is not disliked to separate them because the text came to prohibit separating a minor from a mahram relative. Thus two adults and spouses are not in the scope of the text, so separating them is permissible. It is not permissible to extend the prohibition to them by analogical reasoning because the text came contrary to analogy (qiyas), so it cannot be extended to others by analogy. The proof is that al-Muqawqis al-Qibti sent as a gift to the Prophet (peace be upon him) Mariyah and Sirin, and they were sisters. The Prophet separated them by taking Mariyah as a concubine and giving the other to Hassan, contrary to Muhammad's view. (al-'Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This is a detailed passage on the prohibition of separating close relatives when selling them or disposing of them. The primary proof is the hadith from Abu Musa that the Prophet cursed those who separate a mother from her child or a brother from his brother. The ruling applies to Muslims (free, mukatab, or permitted slave), not to disbelievers as they are not obligated by Islamic law. The prohibition covers separation by sale, gift, inheritance division, spoils, or bequest. The prohibition is specifically between a minor (saghir) and a mahram relative (dhi rahim muharram). It does not apply to two adults (kabiran) or spouses (zawjan). The mahram relative must be one with permanent prohibition of marriage (muharram mu'abbad), like father/son, mother/son, brother/brother. It excludes non-blood mahrams (like foster relatives) and non-mahram blood relatives (like cousins). The prohibition lasts until the minor reaches puberty. A condition is that both the minor and the mahram be in the same ownership. If one is owned by a different owner (e.g., the father's son owns one), then selling is allowed because the ownership is separate. Also if separation is due to a legal right like payment for a crime, debt, or return due to defect, it is allowed. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf, the sale is invalid (yafsidu) if it separates blood relatives (qarabat al-wilad, i.e., direct lineage) but valid for others. In another narration from him, it is invalid in all cases. Zufar and the 'three' (likely Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and another) also invalidate the sale entirely. The author then clarifies that the prohibition does not extend to spouses or adults because the text is against analogy (khalaf al-qiyas), so it cannot be extended. Evidence: the Prophet separated the sisters Mariyah and Sirin, one as concubine and one given to Hassan, indicating that adult sisters can be separated. This contradicts Muhammad's view (perhaps Muhammad al-Shaybani thought it invalid). The relied-upon view is that the sale is valid but makruh tahrimi when conditions are met; some say invalid.

Key Terms
ذي رحم محرم (dhi rahim muharram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relationship, e.g., father, mother, brother, sister.
التفريق (tafriq): Separation of family members by sale, gift, etc., which is prohibited for minors and mahrams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on selling a minor slave separately from his mother?
A) The sale is invalid and must be rescinded.
B) The sale is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) The sale is permissible if the mother agrees.
D) The sale is valid only if the minor is above seven years old.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of separating a minor from a mahram relative is established by hadith, but the sale remains valid; the sin is on the seller.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Separating a Minor from a Mahram in Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on separating minor from mahram in sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on separating a minor from a mahram relative in a sale and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the validity of the sale.

Core Idea
Separating a minor from his mahram in sale is disliked but the sale is valid according to Abu Hanifa.

In Hanafi fiqh, selling a minor apart from his or her mahram relative is not outright invalid but carries a degree of legal dislike (karaha). The classical texts present a nuanced discussion, especially regarding conditions, scope, and an intra-madhhab dispute. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and the differences among Hanafi jurists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: selling a minor separately from his or her mahram relative when both are owned by the same seller. The ruling according to Abu Hanifa is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) but the sale is still valid.
The dislike continues until the minor reaches puberty.
2
Note the necessary conditions for the dislike
First, the child must be a minor (whether Muslim or non-Muslim). Second, the other person must be a mahram (a relative with perpetual marriage prohibition, like parent, sibling, child). Third, both must belong to the same owner. Fourth, the separation must not be due to a rightful claim (e.g., debt, crime).
If ownership is separate (e.g., one belongs to the father, the other to his adult son), there is no dislike.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf has two narrations: (1) the sale is invalid (fasid) in cases of blood relation (nasab) but valid otherwise; (2) the sale is invalid in all cases. Zufar and the 'three' (other early Hanafi authorities) agree with the second. Muhammad al-Shaybani held a different view.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's: sale valid but disliked.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The key proof is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) separated two Coptic sisters, Mariya and Sirin, one being a minor (implied) and the other an adult. This shows separation is allowed for adults and, by contrast, disliked for minors. The ruling is specific and cannot be extended by analogy because it is contrary to general analogy.
The text is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
5
Understand why adults and spouses are excluded
The prohibition is limited to the textual case: minor + mahram. Adults and spouses are not within the 'meaning' of the text, so separating them is permissible. Extending prohibition via analogy is invalid because the original ruling is an exception to the general principle.
The Prophet's treatment of Mariya and Sirin confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يكره من البيوع بين صغير وذي رحم محرم منه، بخلاف الكبيرين والزوجين. وذي رحم محرم منه سواء كان صغيراً أو كبيراً، كافراً أو مسلماً، أو أحدهما مسلم والآخر كافر، وهذه الكراهة تمتد إلى البلوغ، والمراد بذي الرحم المحرم ما كانت القرابة فيه مؤبدة بالمحرمية، مثل الأب والابن، والأم والابن، والأخوين، فلا يدخل فيه محرم غير قريب ولا قريب غير محرم، ثم لابد من اجتماعهما في ملكه، حتى لو كان أحدهما له، والآخر لابنه الصغير، له أن يبيع أحدهما لتفرق الملك، وكذلك لو كان التفريق بحق مستحق عليه كدفع أحدهما بالجناية، وبيع أحدهما بالدين ورده بالعيب وعن أبي يوسف أنه يفسد البيع في قرابة الولاد، ويجوز في غيرها، وعنه أنه يفسد في الجميع لما روينا، وبه قال زفر والثلاثة. بخلاف الكبيرين والزوجين سواء كانا صغيرين أو لا، فإنه لا يكره تفريقهما؛ لأن النص ورد في منع تفريق صغير عن ذي رحم محرم منه، فالكبيران والزوجان ليسا في معنى المنصوص عليه، فيجوز تفريقهما، ولا يجوز أن يثبت فيهما المنع إلحاقاً بالمنصوص عليه بالدلالة؛ لأن النص ورد على خلاف القياس، فلا يلحق به غيره بالدلالة، أن المقوقس القبطي أهدى له مارية وسيرين و كانتا أختين، ففرق بينهما حيث تسرى بمارية، وقد صح وأعطى الأخرى لحسان خلافا لمحمد. (عيني، فتح)
What is disliked of sales: [selling separately] a minor and his mahram relative, unlike two adults and spouses. And a mahram relative is whether [the minor] is small or big, disbeliever or Muslim, or one of them Muslim and the other disbeliever. This dislike extends until puberty. What is meant by mahram relative is one whose relationship is permanently connected by prohibition, like father and son, mother and son, two brothers. It does not include a non-relative who is mahram nor a relative who is not mahram. Then they must be together in his ownership, so if one belongs to him and the other to his minor son, he may sell one of them because of separate ownership. Likewise if the separation is due to a right owed, like handing over one for a crime, or selling one for debt or returning due to defect. And from Abu Yusuf: it invalidates the sale in blood relation and is permitted in other than that. And from him [another narration]: it invalidates in all cases based on what we narrated, and Zufar and the three agree. Unlike two adults and two spouses, whether both are small or not, for it is not disliked to separate them, because the text came prohibiting separation of a minor from his mahram relative. So two adults and spouses are not within the meaning of the text, so it is permissible to separate them. It is not permissible to prove prohibition on them by analogizing to the textual case because the text came contrary to analogy, so no other case is attached to it by analogy. That the Coptic Muqawqis gifted to him [the Prophet] Mariya and Sirin, and they were sisters, and he separated them by taking Mariya as a concubine, and it is authentic, and he gave the other to Hassan. Contrary to Muhammad.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on separating a minor from his mahram relative in a sale. It is a disliked act (makruh) and this dislike continues until the minor reaches puberty. The key condition is that both must be owned by the same person; if ownership is separate, such as one belonging to the father and the other to the son, selling one is permissible. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf has two narrations—one that the sale is invalid (fasad) only when the relationship is through birth (nasab) and valid otherwise, and another that it is invalid in all cases. Zufar and the three (likely the three other imams or the other Hanafi scholars) agree with the second narration. The text clarifies that the prohibition only applies to minors and mahram relatives, not to adults or spouses, because the textual evidence (hadith) is specific and not subject to analogy. The proof cited is the incident where the Prophet separated the two Coptic sisters, Mariya and Sirin, giving one to himself and the other to Hassan ibn Thabit, indicating that separation is allowed for adults. Muhammad al-Shaybani differed on this point.

Key Terms
ذي رحم محرم (dhi rahm mahram): A relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (mahram) due to blood relation, such as father, son, brother.
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike, a legal category between mubah and haram. Here it is tanzihiyya (not tahrimi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not disliked to separate two adults who are mahram (e.g., two adult brothers) in a sale?
A) Because adults are not considered mahram.
B) Because the only textual prohibition is for minors, and the ruling cannot be extended by analogy since it is contrary to analogy.
C) Because adults can consent to separation.
D) Because the hadith specifically permits it for adults.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that separating a minor from his mahram in a sale is makruh tanzih, but the sale is valid, and this ruling is specific to minors and cannot be extended to adults or spouses by analogy.
